<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/13986510-sinead" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/users/1447866690i/13986510._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" alt="" /></a>

<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/13986510-sinead">Sinead</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It wasn't just that she was mad about being given an order; it was that she was being forced to marry Char when she feared her curse would make his<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It wasn't just that she was mad about being given an order; it was that she was being forced to marry Char when she feared her curse would make his life dangerous. Her curse broke because she refused to obey an order not because she didn't want to do it but because she feared for the life of the man she loved.<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1020088">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020088" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/75857-emma" class="left imgcol" title="Emma"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1305947403p2/75857.jpg" alt="Emma" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1020088?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/75857-emma" class="user" title="Emma">Emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/439100.Ella_Enchanted" title="Hardcover 9780060275105" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/75857-emma?shelf=owned-2015-earlier" class="actionLinkLite">owned-2015-earlier</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1020088">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1775977395224878188">Feminists often denounce traditional fairy tales because they perpetuate the ideals of a patriarchal society by encouraging girls to behave like proper princesses and wait for charming princes to take charge and save the day. In response to these traditional fairy tales, many authors have tried to reclaim the realm of fairy tales for girls. These retellings feature active protagonists who are not scared of taking charge and do not need princes to save them. One example of this new fairy tale gen</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1775977395224878188">Feminists often denounce traditional fairy tales because they perpetuate the ideals of a patriarchal society by encouraging girls to behave like proper princesses and wait for charming princes to take charge and save the day. In response to these traditional fairy tales, many authors have tried to reclaim the realm of fairy tales for girls. These retellings feature active protagonists who are not scared of taking charge and do not need princes to save them. One example of this new fairy tale genre is the 1998 children’s novel "Ella Enchanted" by Gail Carson Levine, which takes an untraditional approach to retelling the story of Cinderella. The novel addresses several specific feminist issues, specifically negotiating and fighting the burden of obedience, the importance of female friendships and, of course, learning to save yourself.<br /><br />The story is set in an imaginary, medieval-esque kingdom called Frell. A roaming fairy named Lucinda gives Ella the gift/curse of obedience at Ella’s birth. As a result, Ella has to do everything she is told, no matter what harm it might cause to herself or others. (In the novel, the severity of Ella’s curse in constantly underscored with passages explaining how little control Ella has over her own life: “If someone told me to hop on one foot for a day and a half, I’d have to do it. And hopping on one foot wasn’t the worst order I could be given. If you commanded me to cut off my own head, I’d have to do it.") As the plot moves forward Ella is compelled to leave home to try and find Lucinda and ask her to lift the curse. Along the way she also falls in love with Prince Char. For varying reasons, depending on the version, Lucinda refuses to lift the curse. Further difficulties arise as Ella continues her quest.<br /><br />That's the main body of the story. The Cinderella element is relevant mainly to the last quarter of the novel where actual elements from that story (the slipper, the ball) appear in the story, although the evil step-sisters and fairy godmother are present throughout the narrative. <br /><br /> There are several reasons that I love this novel and recommend it to everyone. The first is that it's an imaginative retelling of Cinderella which makes the story exciting for readers familiar with the original version without making it too abtruse for readers who have never heard of Cinderella. Also, the book is full of great role models for girls. All of the female characters are strong, self-aware women--things seen far too rarely in the fairy tale genre. The novel is narrated in Ella's voice. This makes it easy to see how strong Ella is as a character (especially at the end of the novel). <br /><br />The other great thing about this book is that it all seems authentic, never over the top or under-written. In addition to creating immensely likable main characters, Levine creates a compelling world within the pages of "Ella Enchanted" vivid with details ranging from Elvish and Gnomish languages to customs at a Giant's wedding. The story is an immensely entertaining page-turner that will (even better) leave readers feeling satisfied when they reach the final scene where Levine ties everything together, artfully blending empowerment with a happy-ever-after ending fit for a traditional fairy tale. <br /><br />Excerpted from a scholarly article I wrote about Ella Enchanted as a book and movie. You can read the full article here: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://digitalcommons.pace.edu/research_awards/1/" target="_blank">http://digitalcommons.pace.edu/resear...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1775977395224878188">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_51295586">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51295586" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1876075-cara" class="left imgcol" title="Cara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" alt="Cara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/51295586?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1876075-cara" class="user" title="Cara">Cara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cara by: </span>
      Valerie (sister) and Ginny (friend)
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=books-made-into-movies" class="actionLinkLite">books-made-into-movies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fairy-tales" class="actionLinkLite">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=recommended-to-me" class="actionLinkLite">recommended-to-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer51295586">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4760582835133332075">Now I know why people made such a fuss when the movie came out. I watched the movie first, so I had no idea how utterly wrong everything was. It totally is not like the book. Just slap on the names and the curse and that's where the similarities end. I must say the book is <u> MUCH </u> better than the movie.<br /><br />The style of the writing was kind of weird for me, but not in a bad way. It's not that it was too fast paced or anything, but I noticed there wasn't a lot of padding or fanfare before events would</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4760582835133332075">Now I know why people made such a fuss when the movie came out. I watched the movie first, so I had no idea how utterly wrong everything was. It totally is not like the book. Just slap on the names and the curse and that's where the similarities end. I must say the book is <u> MUCH </u> better than the movie.<br /><br />The style of the writing was kind of weird for me, but not in a bad way. It's not that it was too fast paced or anything, but I noticed there wasn't a lot of padding or fanfare before events would happen, which I usually expect from fantasy books. The writing style worked in this story since it seemed to fit the main character to a tee.<br /><br />I absolutely loved the story. It's a great way of showing how the only one who can save you is you, and you have to find the strength within to do it. Sometimes it takes someone else to bring that strength out of you and that's what Char does for Ella unknowingly.<br /><br />The magic book was a nice touch and added what the other characters were thinking without actually changing the narrator of the story. I couldn't give the book 5 stars because it seemed odd to me how she dealt with her mother's death. It's like after awhile it doesn't seem to matter, which I guess makes sense since the book isn't really about her grieving for her mother. The story is really about how her death makes Ella have to face her demons by throwing her the different situations she finds herself in. Still, it really isn't that bothersome because of course you see that Ella misses her mother at times. <br /><br />This is the best version of the Cinderella story I have encountered. All and all a very worth while read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4760582835133332075">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1820621040564448074">This still stands as one of my favorite books. The fantasy elements are clever and not too over the top. Ella is witty and pretty clever herself, not to mention strong and determined and resourceful. Mandy is just your everyday, ordinary, regular old cook/fairy. Char is, appropriately, charming. The stepsisters are deliciously evil. Lucinda is completely batty.<br /><br />I like that none of the women in the book are doormats. Good or evil, protagonist or minor background character, they have an opinion, th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1820621040564448074">This still stands as one of my favorite books. The fantasy elements are clever and not too over the top. Ella is witty and pretty clever herself, not to mention strong and determined and resourceful. Mandy is just your everyday, ordinary, regular old cook/fairy. Char is, appropriately, charming. The stepsisters are deliciously evil. Lucinda is completely batty.<br /><br />I like that none of the women in the book are doormats. Good or evil, protagonist or minor background character, they have an opinion, they exert at least some control over their own destiny, they are quietly secure in the knowledge of their own power.<br /><br />The movie was terrible, folks, so don't go by that. (Anne Hathaway, why must you insist in being in movies that ruin my favorite kids books?)</span>

  <a href="/user/show/111921-madeline" class="left imgcol" title="Madeline"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" alt="Madeline" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62995265?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 10, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/111921-madeline" class="user" title="Madeline">Madeline</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">kids-and-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62995265">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer744192340134207302">I never liked Cinderella as a kid. It seemed like whenever she got into trouble, her best plan was to burst into tears and wait for someone to come along and help her. I also wondered, even if she couldn't leave her stepmother's house, could she at least tell the awful woman to go make her own damn breakfast once in a while? As far as little cynical-as-hell Madeline was concerned, Cinderella was a spineless twinkie who was painfully useless. <br /><br />Obviously, I am not the only girl who had a problem wi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText744192340134207302">I never liked Cinderella as a kid. It seemed like whenever she got into trouble, her best plan was to burst into tears and wait for someone to come along and help her. I also wondered, even if she couldn't leave her stepmother's house, could she at least tell the awful woman to go make her own damn breakfast once in a while? As far as little cynical-as-hell Madeline was concerned, Cinderella was a spineless twinkie who was painfully useless. <br /><br />Obviously, I am not the only girl who had a problem with the fairy tale, and fortunately, Gail Carson Levine decided to do something about it. Her Cinderella (Ella of Frell) is smart, stubborn, and pretty damn feisty. Her only problem is that when she was born, a well-meaning fairy gave her the gift of obedience. Ella has to obey any direct order given to her, no matter what. So, naturally, she sets out to find the fairy, lift the curse, get rid of her stepmother and stepsisters, and maybe even end up with Prince Char. (Char as in Charmont, geddit?) A lovely story, and much better than anything Disney could come up with.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="744192340134207302">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1172981783">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1172981783" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11375137-cait-grace" class="left imgcol" title="Cait Grace"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1356324709p2/11375137.jpg" alt="Cait Grace" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1172981783?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11375137-cait-grace" class="user" title="Cait Grace">Cait Grace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11375137-cait-grace?shelf=middle-grade" class="actionLinkLite">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11375137-cait-grace?shelf=magical-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11375137-cait-grace?shelf=3-star" class="actionLinkLite">3-star</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11375137-cait-grace?shelf=retelling" class="actionLinkLite">retelling</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11375137-cait-grace?shelf=read-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1172981783">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18273998550639456287"><strong>I was nervous to read this because it's like everyone's Childhood Favourite Book.</strong> GAH! No pressure! I'm 21. So maybe a little over the age range? But I always believe a good book can be appreciated by ANYONE. And I'm right! <strong>This is a good book and I had a great time...but I don't call it a favourite.</strong> I'm sure I would've been absolutely cuddling it when I was 12.<br /><br /><strong>I really liked the 2nd half. The first half? Not so much.</strong> I found it a little telling-ish and not showing-ish. That bugs me. The style i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18273998550639456287"><strong>I was nervous to read this because it's like everyone's Childhood Favourite Book.</strong> GAH! No pressure! I'm 21. So maybe a little over the age range? But I always believe a good book can be appreciated by ANYONE. And I'm right! <strong>This is a good book and I had a great time...but I don't call it a favourite.</strong> I'm sure I would've been absolutely cuddling it when I was 12.<br /><br /><strong>I really liked the 2nd half. The first half? Not so much.</strong> I found it a little telling-ish and not showing-ish. That bugs me. The style isn't my favourite (even though it's 1st person) and I was just SO FRUSTRATED with all the bullying Ella went through. But hellooooo that is the point of the story. I'm not marking it lower for me being frustrated! I'm just saying how I felt. I also felt old and kind of detatched and the passages where they spoke in gobbly-gook in ogre language just had me wondering if the author slapped the keyboard for the phrases or if there was rhyme and reason. (I'm <em>joking</em>. I'm sure there was actually a pattern behind that language. I just...didn't see it.)<br /><br /><strong>It's a fairy-tale retelling of CinderELLA.</strong> Obviously. The beginning feels quite different, but by the end, we roll in the pumpkin and the prince (whose name is "Charm" I SEE WHAT YOU DID THERE, AUTHOR. I DO). <br /><img width="220" height="260" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421665309ra/13400941.gif" /><br />This part was all a bit predictable, but, 'scuse me, but I got all into the smushy romance and shipped Charm and Ella very hard. THEY WERE SO CUTE AND DOOMED FOR SADNESS AND FAILURE. I always get onboard with a doomed couple. :')<br /><br /><strong>I also felt the antagonist was wrapped up very very easily.</strong> There was barely a climax! I realise it's a fairy tale but COME ON. No ogre attack? not even...eh, I don't know...a stepsister setting Ella's dress on fire or something? (Gawsh, Cait, your psychopath is showing.) But everything seemed to wither into this perfect bow and there was literally nothing stopping the happily ever after. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Like even the psychotic fairy godmother was just like "omigosh I have been doing bad things! I'll stop! I'll stop!" and she wasn't even secretly Maleficent-like or anything. And I was SUPER disappointed in Mandy. She did nothing. Basically NOTHING the whole book except be a surrogate mother. If you were a fairy with the ability to do magic, don't you think you'd at least work for yourself instead of being a kitchen slave???.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><strong>So yes, I thought it was cute and good and sweet....but I was a little detached.</strong> I shipped the ship and I did a polka at the ball when things went my way. I wanted to punch the step-sisters and I wanted to speak Ogre with a "oeeehhhel jfiiiiolllk jfidddddi". (That totally means "I didn't understand the freaking ogres, but I appreciate their contribution to the story as ugly large man-eating villains".)<br /><img width="320" height="180" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421665309ra/13400942.gif" /><br /><br />I'm definitely glad I read it!<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18273998550639456287">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2008" class="actionLinkLite">2008</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=fairytales" class="actionLinkLite">fairytales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer16627345">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3775122608845814085">It's a sweet, humorous book, written for a younger audience but easily enjoyed by an older one too. Based on the Cinderella story, there are a few notable differences, namely that Ella was "blessed" with the "gift" of obedience by the fairy Lucinda, who thinks all her gifts (such as turning you into a squirrel) are wonderful. Ella is the daughter of Lady Eleanor and a somewhat unscrupulous merchant, Sir Peter, whom she rarely sees. She grows up with her mother, who teaches her to slide down the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3775122608845814085">It's a sweet, humorous book, written for a younger audience but easily enjoyed by an older one too. Based on the Cinderella story, there are a few notable differences, namely that Ella was "blessed" with the "gift" of obedience by the fairy Lucinda, who thinks all her gifts (such as turning you into a squirrel) are wonderful. Ella is the daughter of Lady Eleanor and a somewhat unscrupulous merchant, Sir Peter, whom she rarely sees. She grows up with her mother, who teaches her to slide down the banister, and the cook Mandy, who's not all she seems. She learns fairly early what a curse the gift is, where any command must be obeyed. The opportunities for being taken advantage of are mind-boggling (but strictly G-rated). Ella learns to be defiant even while she is forced to obey, but the trick doesn't always work.<br /><br />When, at fifteen, her mother dies several things happen. Firstly, she meets Prince Char and forms a friendship with him, and secondly her father decides to send her to finishing school along with the two hideous daughters of Dame Olga, who has her sights set on Sir Peter. The daughters, Hattie and Olive, are greedy, rude and obnoxious, but things become worse when Hattie realises Ella must obey her.<br /><br />Ella is desperate to find Lucinda and have her remove the curse, which leads her to run away from the finishing school and into all sorts of trouble. Unlike a lot of fantasy stories, though, this one isn't a quest story set on an endless road. Ella meets Elves and is nearly eaten by Ogres, but spends most of the story at home. Humorous escapades and a blooming friendship between her and Char balance out the cruelty dealt her by others. And the Cinderella aspect is given full due, but in a refreshing way. The similarities are there, but it never feels old and tired and same-y. <br /><br />Also, Ella herself is a great heroine, smart and strong but not over-confident or perfect. She's a bit clumsy but has the gift of imitating languages and voices, and learning languages quickly. She's no defenceless damsel and she doesn't whinge, but her curse curtails who she really is. The moral of the story is fitting, but not lecturing. Levine has a much lighter hand than your average Disney movie, and there's not a saccharine moment. It reminds me a bit of the movie <em>Ever After</em>, so if you liked that then you'll like this book, and vice versa.<br /><br />A joy to read, and very well written, <em>Ella Enchanted</em> took up a few hours of my time but will take up a much larger slice of my memory: for making me laugh at the end of an exhausting week, for being sweet but not cloying, wise but not preachy, and for revitalising an old fairytale.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3775122608845814085">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of princess and fairy tales</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/142816-heavyreader?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer37607950">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10524398313759188347">My sister recommended this book to me and even bought me a copy at half price day at Goodwill. Now I am recommending this book to you. <br /><br />The main character, Ella, is a young woman, almost 15, who is cursed with obedience as an infant. A fairy thinks she's blessing the baby by forcing her to be obedient, but that's not really how it turns out. Imagine being physically compelled to do <em>anything</em> that <em>anyone</em> tells you to do. You don't have to be an anarchist to quickly realize that would be a rotten wa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10524398313759188347">My sister recommended this book to me and even bought me a copy at half price day at Goodwill. Now I am recommending this book to you. <br /><br />The main character, Ella, is a young woman, almost 15, who is cursed with obedience as an infant. A fairy thinks she's blessing the baby by forcing her to be obedient, but that's not really how it turns out. Imagine being physically compelled to do <em>anything</em> that <em>anyone</em> tells you to do. You don't have to be an anarchist to quickly realize that would be a rotten way to live. <br /><br />Thankfully, Ella is intelligent, clever, witty, and gifted with languages. <br /><br />After a family tragedy, the previously sheltered Ella is forced out into the world where she goes on a quest to find the fairy who cursed her and ask for relief from her burden.<br /><br />Two-thirds of the way through, the book becomes the retelling of the classic Cinderella story. At first I was nervous that the great beginning of the book would be ruined by this quirky turn, but it actually worked out really well.<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine is a gifted writer, and I enjoyed this story immensely. I recommend this book for little girls and really anyone all into "someday my prince will come" and "happily ever after." This feisty heroine will be an inspiration to everyone who reads her story</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10524398313759188347">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_60254354">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60254354" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/306690-jacki" class="left imgcol" title="Jacki"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1366077657p2/306690.jpg" alt="Jacki" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/60254354?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 08, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/306690-jacki" class="user" title="Jacki">Jacki</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10338023-ella-enchanted" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/306690-jacki?shelf=young-adult-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer60254354">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1867474521699785207">I felt like the author said to herself: "I'm going to really revamp the Cinderella classic! I'm gonna give the girl a backstory like you wouldn't believe! and it's going to be cute, and funny, and there will be all kinds of mythical creatures in it! It's going to be wholly other-worldly! And she's going to go on this awesome journey that's going to be epic and life changing!"<br /><br />All that ended halfway through the book: The journey, the special creatures, the seemingly important gifts and details, th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1867474521699785207">I felt like the author said to herself: "I'm going to really revamp the Cinderella classic! I'm gonna give the girl a backstory like you wouldn't believe! and it's going to be cute, and funny, and there will be all kinds of mythical creatures in it! It's going to be wholly other-worldly! And she's going to go on this awesome journey that's going to be epic and life changing!"<br /><br />All that ended halfway through the book: The journey, the special creatures, the seemingly important gifts and details, the developmental steps... all gone. And then the author thought to herself, "Oh wait...this is supposed to be Cinderella. Um..let's see...her father remarries...her stepfamily hates her...turns her into a slave...glass slippers...the prince has a ball...glass slippers...they get married...The end!"<br /><br />So really the book is two stories. The totally awesome cool story that the author started with...and the cliche, not-at-all-revamped Cinderella story that she ended with. <br /><br />And for Goodness Sakes! WHAT WAS WITH THE ELVES GIFTS?! She made it seem so damn important that we should know about these gifts and all the way through the novel Ella is hiding them and they're special and they're everything her father ever wanted...<br />What happens to them?!<br />We don't know! <br />She kept them in a bag for the rest of her life!<br />AND THE NECKLACE?! I thought for sure that was going to be the key to everything! It was special and important when it was introduced. it was an heirloom. It was gnome-made (gnomes are magic). It's stolen from her. She wants it back. She contemplates getting it back...<br />Then for the next hundred pages, it's never mentioned, but suddenly at the end of the book, *poof* she has it back. All is well. The End.<br /><br />GAH!<br /><br />I still enjoyed the book, but good grief, make a tighter story, Lady!<br /><br />by the way:<br />Prince Charming<br />Prince Charmonte<br />...hmmm....<br />I don't like that kind of blaring twist on cliches. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_165122436">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165122436" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5304659-veronica" class="left imgcol" title="Veronica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1303588479p2/5304659.jpg" alt="Veronica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/165122436?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 04, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5304659-veronica" class="user" title="Veronica">Veronica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer165122436">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7943035182513546798">When some of my friends learned I was reading <em> Ella Enchanted</em> for the very first time, the first thing they told me was, "What! I read that book, like, when I was in fifth grade!" Well, let me just say, I wouldn't have enjoyed this book in fifth grade as I have enjoyed it now. It's exactly what one of my bookworm friends would have described as a "cookie read": short, sweet, and satisfactory. It was a truly well-woven, fanciful tale with just the right pint of humor, a delightful sprinkling of r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7943035182513546798">When some of my friends learned I was reading <em> Ella Enchanted</em> for the very first time, the first thing they told me was, "What! I read that book, like, when I was in fifth grade!" Well, let me just say, I wouldn't have enjoyed this book in fifth grade as I have enjoyed it now. It's exactly what one of my bookworm friends would have described as a "cookie read": short, sweet, and satisfactory. It was a truly well-woven, fanciful tale with just the right pint of humor, a delightful sprinkling of romance, a delectable amount of fantasy sugar dust, and what makes a simple story so memorable: the ability to evoke small pinpricks of pain in a reader's chest when we realize something in life holds us beneath a curse, and the unmistakable taste of that stirring moment of victory when we find new strength along the way to break the curse and become free.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7943035182513546798">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1157294968?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/947145-janessa" class="user" title="Janessa">Janessa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/947145-janessa?shelf=middle-grade" class="actionLinkLite">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1157294968">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer600299691410259561">This book gets five huge, shiny stars because of the following conversation I had with my 12 year old today:<br /><br />"Mom, Kate (name changed) was teasing me at school today, but I don't think it was friendly teasing. I think it was mean."<br /><br />"It probably was mean." (We've had a lot of problems with Kate bossing and teasing lately, but my daughter is always anxious to give Kate the benefit of the doubt). <br /><br />After a moment's thought, my daughter said, "It's like Ella Enchanted - how she has to listen to mean peo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText600299691410259561">This book gets five huge, shiny stars because of the following conversation I had with my 12 year old today:<br /><br />"Mom, Kate (name changed) was teasing me at school today, but I don't think it was friendly teasing. I think it was mean."<br /><br />"It probably was mean." (We've had a lot of problems with Kate bossing and teasing lately, but my daughter is always anxious to give Kate the benefit of the doubt). <br /><br />After a moment's thought, my daughter said, "It's like Ella Enchanted - how she has to listen to mean people and do what they say. Only I don't have to listen to Kate or do what she says because I don't have a spell cast on me like Ella does. I'm not going to listen to Kate anymore. I'll still be nice, but I'm going to step back."<br /><br />Thank you, Gail Carson Levine, for crafting an empowering story for girls, and for helping my daughter see, through the lens of Ella's experiences, that always trying to conform to others can be like living with a curse. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="600299691410259561">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_110567059">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110567059" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3284904-jasmin" class="left imgcol" title="Jasmin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1351874823p2/3284904.jpg" alt="Jasmin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/110567059?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 10, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3284904-jasmin" class="user" title="Jasmin">Jasmin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All the little girls and the little girls at heart</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=fairy-tale" class="actionLinkLite">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=reviewed-by-me" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed-by-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer110567059">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer705822740365681770">Unicorns. Fairies. Castles. Most of all, Prince Charming.<br /><br />Ella Enchanted made me want to revert back to being a little girl, where it's easy to believe that happily ever afters do exist. And yes, it reminded me that, despite my bitter self now, I at one point, believed in happily ever afters.<br /><br />Who doesn't know Ella? I sure caught the craze when this was a movie with Anne Hathaway as Ella. The movie was spectacular, and the book was just as good.<br /><br />Ella was bestowed the gift of obedience. Well, to the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText705822740365681770">Unicorns. Fairies. Castles. Most of all, Prince Charming.<br /><br />Ella Enchanted made me want to revert back to being a little girl, where it's easy to believe that happily ever afters do exist. And yes, it reminded me that, despite my bitter self now, I at one point, believed in happily ever afters.<br /><br />Who doesn't know Ella? I sure caught the craze when this was a movie with Anne Hathaway as Ella. The movie was spectacular, and the book was just as good.<br /><br />Ella was bestowed the gift of obedience. Well, to the fairy who dared to give it, it was a gift. But to the other end who received it, it was definitely a curse. Ella made me laugh. But she also made my heart break. I could not imagine myself doing everything someone ordered me to do. Even the simple task of following parents seemed Herculean, when your heart had no desire to do it. But Ella had to do every blasted thing. Whether, she liked it or not, she had to obey. She could try delaying tactics, but in the end, the curse will always get the best of her.<br /><br />But despite the crazed obedience, Ella was still a girl. Charming. Humorous. Intellectual. Unselfish. Patient. And courageous. And a prince could not help but notice her.<br /><br />Prince Char, after having friendship with Ella, proposes. But Ella could not risk being the Prince's downfall. Once enemies knew of her affliction, one could not help but to take advantage. So Ella tricked the prince into thinking she had married another.<br /><br />But true love could not be stopped.<br /><br />As the town was to hold series of balls, where rumor has it, the prince would choose a bride, Ella could not help but rush off, and maybe see the prince once more. She poses as Lela, and again, she has caught the eye of the prince.<br /><br />But just as Cinderella did, Ella had to leave, as soon as the prince found her true identity.<br /><br />Ella could not even consider harming the prince, despite all the love she had in her heart for him. The prince orders her to marry him, but with the thought of his imminent danger, she manages to fight of the curse with an extreme amount of disobedience. <br /><br />Well, of course, now that she's no threat to the prince anymore, evidently, they could now have their happily ever after.<br /><br />This book makes me want to believe in happily ever afters once more. Maybe I will, but I would rather wait for it to come, and see for myself ?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="705822740365681770">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5509745440096781582">If you've seen the movie without reading the book, YOU ARE MISSING OUT! If you haven't seen the movie, make sure you read the book before you do, and I hope you do (well, at least read the book). The book explores the life of a girl growing up in the times of fairies and ogres, giants and elves, and let's not forget the evil stepmother and stepsister! Ella is a smart girl with a curse. At her birth a fairy gave Ella the "gift" of obedience. Immediately, this proves to be a bad gift. If someone w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5509745440096781582">If you've seen the movie without reading the book, YOU ARE MISSING OUT! If you haven't seen the movie, make sure you read the book before you do, and I hope you do (well, at least read the book). The book explores the life of a girl growing up in the times of fairies and ogres, giants and elves, and let's not forget the evil stepmother and stepsister! Ella is a smart girl with a curse. At her birth a fairy gave Ella the "gift" of obedience. Immediately, this proves to be a bad gift. If someone were to tell Ella to chop off her head, she would have to do it! Join Ella in her journey through life, learning, loyalty, and of course, love. Once again, please read this book; the movie is entertaining, but does it no justice.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/45508990?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 05, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1985596-laura-spaulding" class="user" title="Laura Spaulding">Laura Spaulding</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45508990">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6457214646837583580">This was my absolute favorite book when I was a kid. I still have my first copy of it; the poor thing is so tattered and yellowed. It's a story about a girl placed under a spell by a fairy at birth and the journey she goes on to rid herself of the curse. Fairies, trolls, evil step mothers, magic-you name it, this book has it. I <strong>refuse</strong> to see the disney movie version. The book (although a fairy tale) was rather dark (death, curses, evil people, ect), and i'm sure disney completely butchered that.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/51635825?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 12, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1884487-ash" class="user" title="Ash">Ash</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Paperback 9780590920681" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ash by: </span>
      Cara and Valerie
  </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer51635825">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7296900176573390115"> This was a very sweet and funny book. The movie version really doesn't do it justice and is almost a different story all together. I'd always heard about this book when I was in elementary and middle school, but back then I thought reading a book was punishment. Now though, I see that books are our friends and not just good paper weights. I'm glad that I had a chance to read this book before I got too old to actually enjoy it. Though I think that I would've still liked it anyway. Ella is funny</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7296900176573390115"> This was a very sweet and funny book. The movie version really doesn't do it justice and is almost a different story all together. I'd always heard about this book when I was in elementary and middle school, but back then I thought reading a book was punishment. Now though, I see that books are our friends and not just good paper weights. I'm glad that I had a chance to read this book before I got too old to actually enjoy it. Though I think that I would've still liked it anyway. Ella is funny and witty and not much like the girl on the cover. It was easy to see the frustration and anger that Ella felt whenever she had to obey a command that she didn't willingly do. The gift of constant obedience really is a curse. I can't imagine having to always do what I'm told. I hate it when people tell me what to do! It's easy to sympathize with Ella, you root for her from the beginning all the way to the end. She's strong willed even with her curse, which gets her into trouble at times. I loved the fact that the book wasn't all about some beautiful girl and how she eventually snagged the prince...The End. It was about how we all have the strength inside of us to do even what seems impossible.<br /><br /> I think that I would have enjoyed this book a lot more when I was a few years younger. The charm of it all didn't capture me as much as it would have if I were 13 or 14. I'm not sure if it was the cover that threw me off, but at the very beginning I kept imagining Ella to be around 12 years old when she was actually 15. Maybe it was because at the beginning some of her thoughts sounded like they were from someone younger. Eventually I got it right though. I think younger girls would really enjoy this book, but anyone could read it and still like it. A very nice story. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7296900176573390115">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12987078847076597659">Squeeeeeeeeeeeee!!! I have a new favourite now, oh my. :D Why did it take me so long to read this?! Maybe because the book itself is a falling-apart ex-library hardcover, that just looks so unappealing.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText12987078847076597659">Squeeeeeeeeeeeee!!! I have a new favourite now, oh my. :D Why did it take me so long to read this?! Maybe because the book itself is a falling-apart ex-library hardcover, that just looks so unappealing. Tch. :P Each time Solyndra has mentioned it I've thought I should really read it at last, so good thing THIS time I finally DID.<br /><br />SO MUCH LOVE. The whole story is just marvellous and wonderful. I was so invested in the Ella/Char romance and it takes a lot for me to actually, seriously, deeply CARE to the point of wanting to cry/sigh when it's a boy-girl relationship! This book truly is something special. Hattie is so horrible I want to throttle her - especially when she forbade Ella being friends with Areida, I wanted to CRY!! Thank goodness Ella ran away before she could hurt Areida, I was so upset over that. :( And Char was just wonderful, and the balls were wonderful, and the Cinderella-ness of the story was charming... *sighs* I do want to read it again and again!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer513236373">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16842099644479038759"><strong>How can a fairy’s blessing be such a pain in the ass?</strong><br /><br />On a wonderful morning in a land of Frell, a beautiful baby was born, her name's Ella. Having been born that beautiful morning became a disaster to Ella and her mother as a foolish fairy gave Ella the gift of "obedience". Well, that doesn't sound bad, doesn't it? The twist is, having the gift of "obedience" means that she has to do whatever a random person tells her to do, like chopping her head for instance! Ella, on the other hand, does not</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16842099644479038759"><strong>How can a fairy’s blessing be such a pain in the ass?</strong><br /><br />On a wonderful morning in a land of Frell, a beautiful baby was born, her name's Ella. Having been born that beautiful morning became a disaster to Ella and her mother as a foolish fairy gave Ella the gift of "obedience". Well, that doesn't sound bad, doesn't it? The twist is, having the gift of "obedience" means that she has to do whatever a random person tells her to do, like chopping her head for instance! Ella, on the other hand, does not accept her fate. So against all odds, she enters an adventure in search of the foolish fairy that can take out the <s>blessing</s> curse. XD<br /><br />Ella Enchanted was my favorite elementary romance-princess novel! The characters, setting, story are all believable and likable. I would like to read this elementary princess novel again! ;)<br /><br /></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4086821009897385703">TBR Reduce Challenge #24- 2011 (Morgan)<br /><br /><em>And so, with laugher and love, we lived happily ever after</em><br /><br />...it's been a <em>long time</em> since I've read this kind of ending;) lol<br /><br />I really wish I was into book when I was younger. I think this book would have been one of my all time favorites growing up. At last, I've seen the movie before even knowing this was a book so I missed out. I can see what everyone is on about. This was so much better then the movie!<br /><br /><strong>Ella Enchanted</strong> is what fairy tales are made of and I thoroughly enjoyed seeing the differences between movie and book and was very surprised <em>just</em> how totally different they were. <br /><br />Perfect for any age! Fun! Sweet! Loved it!</span>

      <a href="/user/show/18116666-ruchama-feuerman" class="user" title="Ruchama Feuerman">Ruchama Feuerman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer799022797">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12131781207974502729">One of the reviewers on GR said, (sort of): "Don't look for hidden meaning or depth,just read it for what it is, a cute fairy tale." But re-reading this book, what I loved most were the witty letters exchanged between Ella and Prince Char, which captured the excitement and thrill of an old-fashioned courtship, the peeling off of mental layers, the wonderful exchange of inquiring (and kind) minds. And when that kiss finally comes, it's obvious that it celebrates this wonderful intimacy between th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12131781207974502729">One of the reviewers on GR said, (sort of): "Don't look for hidden meaning or depth,just read it for what it is, a cute fairy tale." But re-reading this book, what I loved most were the witty letters exchanged between Ella and Prince Char, which captured the excitement and thrill of an old-fashioned courtship, the peeling off of mental layers, the wonderful exchange of inquiring (and kind) minds. And when that kiss finally comes, it's obvious that it celebrates this wonderful intimacy between them, instead of a kiss used to create intimacy -- what we usually get in our modern times. Are there any adult equivalent novels, minus the ogres and fairies? Maybe Jane Eyre.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12131781207974502729">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10188802058128895910">I was recently told that I am too old to be reading "kids books", so I decided to read more. :) <br /><br />I absolutely love that it is basically another retelling of a story I have known by heart since I was a child, and yet it still captivated my attention all the way and made me fall in love with the story in a new way.<br /><br /><br />I now need to be even more of a big kid and watch the movie. </a>

  
<script charset="utf-8" type="text/javascript">
//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EQECIbUO3LwHpGU28ia6BWxHdXwP49ChUXHau69dizp01T3yR9zIRot8EY2MR1y3JbC2ZUY+lws7eN8pY8h9fw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yJT8ErsBlpcB0k1SzIovnFXuGiPuvSEKpqxy7aeQmOOtQMPBSdOCbY0KOemy68kuHBnZOqdgZqDMpXd/awVupg==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13677.Gail_Carson_Levine">About Gail Carson Levine</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/13677.Gail_Carson_Levine"><img alt="13677" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1432495575p2/13677.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer8829522788963251838">Just letting you all know: I'm only going to review books I love. There's enough negative criticism without me piling on. A book is too hard to write.<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine grew up in New York City and began writing seriously in 1987. Her first book for children, Ella Enchanted, was a 1998 Newbery Honor Book. Levine's other books include Fairest; Dave at Night, an ALA Notable Book and Best Book for Yo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8829522788963251838">Just letting you all know: I'm only going to review books I love. There's enough negative criticism without me piling on. A book is too hard to write.<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine grew up in New York City and began writing seriously in 1987. Her first book for children, Ella Enchanted, was a 1998 Newbery Honor Book. Levine's other books include Fairest; Dave at Night, an ALA Notable Book and Best Book for Young Adults; The Wish; The Two Princesses of Bamarre; and the six Princess Tales books. She is also the author of the nonfiction book Writing Magic: Creating Stories That Fly and the picture book Betsy Who Cried Wolf, illustrated by Scott Nash. Gail, her husband, David, and their Airedale, Baxter, live in a 1790 farmhouse in the Hudson River Valley of New York State.</span>
